<script>
//<![CDATA[
      var newTip = new Tip($('bookCover_30735'), "\n\n  <h2><a class=\"readable bookTitle\" href=\"https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/30735.The_Complete_Essays?from_choice=false&amp;from_home_module=false\">The Complete Essays<\/a><\/h2>\n\n      <div>\n        by <a class=\"authorName\" href=\"/author/show/17241.Michel_de_Montaigne?a=9&amp;origin=related_works\">Michel de Montaigne<\/a>\n      <\/div>\n\n          <div class=\"smallText uitext darkGreyText\">\n            <span class=\"minirating\"><span class=\"stars staticStars notranslate\"><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p10\"><\/span><span size=\"12x12\" class=\"staticStar p3\"><\/span><\/span> 4.24 avg rating &mdash; 11,735 ratings<\/span>            &mdash; published 1588\n          <\/div>\n\n    <div class=\"addBookTipDescription\">\n      \n<span id=\"freeTextContainer7041491578645623932\">Michel de Montaigne was one of the most influential figures of the Renaissance, singlehandedly responsible for popularising the essay as a literary form. This Penguin Classics edition of The Complete Essays is translated from the French and edited wi<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText7041491578645623932\" style=\"display:none\">Michel de Montaigne was one of the most influential figures of the Renaissance, singlehandedly responsible for popularising the essay as a literary form. This Penguin Classics edition of The Complete Essays is translated from the French and edited with an introduction and notes by M.A. Screech.\n\nIn 1572 Montaigne retired to his estates in order to devote himself to leisure, reading and reflection. There he wrote his constantly expanding \'assays\', inspired by the ideas he found in books contained in his library and from his own experience. He discusses subjects as diverse as war-horses and cannibals, poetry and politics, sex and religion, love and friendship, ecstasy and experience. But, above all, Montaigne studied himself as a way of drawing out his own inner nature and that of men and women in general. The Essays are among the most idiosyncratic and personal works in all literature and provide an engaging insight into a wise Renaissance mind, continuing to give pleasure and enlightenment to modern readers.\n\nWith its extensive introduction and notes, M.A. Screech\'s edition of Montaigne is widely regarded as the most distinguished of recent times.\n\nMichel de Montaigne (1533-1586) studied law and spent a number of years working as a counsellor before devoting his life to reading, writing and reflection.\n\nIf you enjoyed The Complete Essays, you might like Francois Rabelais\'s Gargantua and Pantagruel, also available in Penguin Classics.\n\n\'Screech\'s fine version ... must surely serve as the definitive English Montaigne\'A.C. He reveals philosophical<\/span>\n  <span id=\"freeText3422698028431653390\" style=\"display:none\">Hegel wrote this classic as an introduction to a series of lectures on the &quot;philosophy of history&quot; — a novel concept in the early nineteenth century. With this work, he created the history of philosophy as a scientific study. He reveals philosophical theory as neither an accident nor an artificial construct, but as an exemplar of its age, fashioned by its antecedents and contemporary circumstances, and serving as a model for the future. The author himself appears to have regarded this book as a popular introduction to his philosophy as a whole, and it remains the most readable and accessible of all his philosophical writings.Eschewing the methods of original history (written during the period in question) and reflective history (written after the period has passed), Hegel embraces philosophic history, which employs a priori philosophical thought to interpret history as a rational process. Reason rules history, he asserts, through its infinite freedom (being self-sufficient, it depends on nothing beyond its own laws and conclusions) and power (through which it forms its own laws). Hegel argues that all of history is caused and guided by a rational process, and God\'s seemingly unknowable plan is rendered intelligible through philosophy. The notion that reason rules the world, he concludes, is both necessary to the practice of philosophic history and a conclusion drawn from that practice.<\/span>\n  <a Is it better thought of as \'true belief\'? Or is it, as many modern philosophers argue, \'justified true belief\', in which the belief is supported by argument or evidence? With skill and eloquence, Socrates guides the debate, drawing out the implications of these theories and subjecting them to merciless and mesmerising criticism.       <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/10994.Blaise_Pascal">About Blaise Pascal</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>
<a href="/author/show/10994.Blaise_Pascal"><div class='bookAuthorProfile__photo' style='background-image: url(https://images.gr-assets.com/authors/1397937717p3/10994.jpg);'></div>
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__name'>
<a href="/author/show/10994.Blaise_Pascal">Blaise Pascal
</a></div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__followerCount'>
563
followers
</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer6508327182687893664">French mathematician and philosopher Blaise Pascal was a contemporary of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36556.Ren__Descartes' title='René Descartes' rel='nofollow noopener'>René Descartes</a> and was ten when <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14190.Galileo_Galilei' title='Galileo Galilei' rel='nofollow noopener'>Galileo Galilei</a> was forced to recant his belief that the earth circled the sun. He and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10122.Thomas_Hobbes' title='Thomas Hobbes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thomas Hobbes</a> lived in Paris at the same time (1640) including the year <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10122.Hobbes' title='Hobbes' rel='nofollow noopener'>Hobbes</a> published his famous <i>Leviathan</i> (1651). Together with <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/380281.Pierre_de_Fermat' title='Pierre de Fermat' rel='nofollow noopener'>Pierre de Fermat</a>, Pascal created the calculus of probabilities.<br/><br/>A near-fatal </span>
  <span id="freeText6508327182687893664" style="display:none">French mathematician and philosopher Blaise Pascal was a contemporary of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/36556.Ren__Descartes" title="René Descartes" rel="nofollow noopener">René Descartes</a> and was ten when <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/14190.Galileo_Galilei" title="Galileo Galilei" rel="nofollow noopener">Galileo Galilei</a> was forced to recant his belief that the earth circled the sun. He and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10122.Thomas_Hobbes" title="Thomas Hobbes" rel="nofollow noopener">Thomas Hobbes</a> lived in Paris at the same time (1640) including the year <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/10122.Hobbes" title="Hobbes" rel="nofollow noopener">Hobbes</a> published his famous <i>Leviathan</i> (1651). Together with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/380281.Pierre_de_Fermat" title="Pierre de Fermat" rel="nofollow noopener">Pierre de Fermat</a>, Pascal created the calculus of probabilities.<br /><br />A near-fatal carriage accident in November 1654 — less than eight years before his death — persuaded him to turn his intellect finally toward religion. The story goes that on the proverbial dark and stormy night, while Pascal was riding in a carriage across a bridge in a Paris suburb, a fright caused the horses to bolt, sending them over the edge. The carriage bearing Pascal survived. Pascal took the incident as a sign and devoted himself to theology. It was at this point that he began writing a series against the Jesuits in 1657 called the <i>Provincial Letters</i>.<br /><br />Pascal is perhaps most famous for his Wager ('Pascal's Wager'), which is not as clear in his language as in this summary: "If Jesus does not exist, the non Christian loses little by believing in him and gains little by not believing. If Jesus does exist, the non Christian gains eternal life by believing and loses an infinite good by not believing.”<br /><br />Sick throughout his life, Pascal died in Paris, probably from a combination of tuberculosis and stomach cancer at age 39. At the last he was a Jansenist Catholic. No one knows if Pascal won his Wager.</span>
  <a data-text-id="6508327182687893664" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
